  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a55defc8-a91c-495c-a3e3-7151b641ad61'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer16006695942386969805">London 1910<br/><br/>Fifteen year-old Belle has lived in a brothel in Seven Dials all her life, with no understanding of what happens in the rooms upstairs. But her innocence is shattered when she witnesses the murder of one of the girls and, subsequently snatched from the streets by the killer, she is sold into prostitution in Paris.<br/><br/>No longer mistress of her own fate, Belle is blow</span>
  <span id="freeText16006695942386969805" style="display:none">London 1910<br /><br />Fifteen year-old Belle has lived in a brothel in Seven Dials all her life, with no understanding of what happens in the rooms upstairs. But her innocence is shattered when she witnesses the murder of one of the girls and, subsequently snatched from the streets by the killer, she is sold into prostitution in Paris.<br /><br />No longer mistress of her own fate, Belle is blown across the globe to sensuous New Orleans where she comes of age and learns to enjoy life as a courtesan. Yet thoughts of home - and the knowledge her status as golden girl cannot last - compel her to break out of her gilded cage.<br /><br />But Belle finds escaping tougher than she imagined, for her life is threatened by desperate men who crave her beauty and attention. Armed only with resourcefulness and spirit, she has a long and dangerous journey ahead of her.<br /><br />Will courage be enough to sustain her? Can she make it back to her family and friends and find her chance at true happiness?</span>

<div id="review_132223081" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132223081" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/546484-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500388520p2/546484.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/132223081?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/546484-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132223081" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10962395752144263007">I have spent the past couple of days immersed in the story of Belle, and have travelled from the slums of Seven Dials in London to New Orleans via Paris with each and every character and place described beautifully and jumping out from the pages. <br/><br/>Lesley Pearse has long been one of my very favourite authors, she is a true storyteller and this is her at her very very best. Belle begins the novel a a somewhat innocent young girl of fifteen, shielded from the murkiness of the world she lives in by h</span>
  <span id="freeText10962395752144263007" style="display:none">I have spent the past couple of days immersed in the story of Belle, and have travelled from the slums of Seven Dials in London to New Orleans via Paris with each and every character and place described beautifully and jumping out from the pages. <br /><br />Lesley Pearse has long been one of my very favourite authors, she is a true storyteller and this is her at her very very best. Belle begins the novel a a somewhat innocent young girl of fifteen, shielded from the murkiness of the world she lives in by her Mother and her housekeeper Mog. This all changes when she finds herself the only witness to a brutal murder, she is snatched from the street and her 'education' into the dark, violent underworld of prostitution and crime begins.<br /><br />The story follows Belle's journey, across the Channel to Paris and then onto New Orleans. Lesley Pearse is the master of strong heroines struggling through difficult circumstances and Belle really is one of the strongest and passionate characters of any of her novels. The horror and violence surrounding the abduction of young girls to satisfy the urges of older, wealthy men is described fully - there are shocking scenes involving not only villainous men but women who think nothing of selling a young girl in order to make more money for themselves. It would be easy to dismiss this as 'just fiction' but it is evident that a lot of research has been done and shocking to think that today, a hundred years later, there are still young girls being sold into the sex trade all over the world.<br /><br />Despite the fact that Belle is almost 600 pages long it really does engage the reader, I found it difficult to put it down as the story is so quickly paced, full of fabulous characters and I was willing Belle along at a every step.<br /><br />Alongside books, shoes are my passion and picking up and reading Belle is like slipping your feet into the most comfortable pair of shoes you've ever found but with the added thrill of those red sparkly high heels.<br /><br />This is romance and history yet contemporary at the same time - a wonderful story. I have enjoyed every one of Lesley's books but really think that this is up there with my favourites - alongside 'Never Look Back'.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10962395752144263007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

(Except Belle did see a cow in the countryside once ...)<br/>- Belle. Was. Annoying. It didn't make sense reading about her supposed uber naivity, then her being super introspective (as though she'd b</span>
  <span id="freeText12197571545451591912" style="display:none">Ugh. <br /><br />Two stars for a good storyline. <br />Less than one star for everything else. <br /><br />My "issues" (because we know I have them)<br />- Set in 1910/ London/ Paris/ New Orleanse. Pearse fell flat by not leveraging the colorful era/ locales instead you really couldn't tell when or where it was until a character told you. (Except Belle did see a cow in the countryside once ...)<br />- Belle. Was. Annoying. It didn't make sense reading about her supposed uber naivity, then her being super introspective (as though she'd been through years of counseling), then her claims of being able to figure people because how observant she was, and then continually dumbly trusting people who most of the time turned out to be awful. What a ding dong. <br />- Too many plot twists. By the end it felt like old seasons of 90210 where you wondered what's the next horrible thing they can make to the same character. <br />- Everything came together too nicely at the end. "Look! everyone found love and is happily ever after!"<br />- Also way too sexually graphic for my liking. Pearse really could've achieved the same awful book without it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12197571545451591912" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1672479603?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie.g" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie.g" href="/user/show/19892876-katie-g">Katie.g</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1672479603" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18368524236327185335">2.5 stars.<br/><br/>Belle had the potential to be so much more. I've read stories before of women going into prostitution and books like Memoirs of a Geisha and Tears of Tess have captured it so much better.<br/><br/>The story itself wasn't bad. If you're looking for an easy read, a story where you can root for the main character and a lighter version of a prostitution story then Belle is your book.<br/><br/>It starts with in the early 1900s in Seven Dials, London. Belle (who was raised in a whorehouse), finally discovers th</span>
  <span id="freeText18368524236327185335" style="display:none">2.5 stars.<br /><br />Belle had the potential to be so much more. I've read stories before of women going into prostitution and books like Memoirs of a Geisha and Tears of Tess have captured it so much better.<br /><br />The story itself wasn't bad. If you're looking for an easy read, a story where you can root for the main character and a lighter version of a prostitution story then Belle is your book.<br /><br />It starts with in the early 1900s in Seven Dials, London. Belle (who was raised in a whorehouse), finally discovers the manner of the work the girls do upstairs by witnessing the murder of one of those girls. In order to keep her silent on the matter, the murderer sells her secretly into prostitution abroad when all she ever wanted to do was run a hat shop. People who care about her including Jimmy, a friend she'd known for literally five minutes are desperate to find her and bring her home.<br /><br />The novel is a tad overlong and filled with almost too many twists and turns. In that regard it reminds me a little of a soap opera. But my biggest source of disbelief with this book (aside from being oblivious from the fact that she lived in a whorehouse) was Belle's unwavering innocence and determination. Despite her harrowing experiences she barely changed throughout. Everyone who knew her for five minutes loved her. She never became bitter or jaded. In fact her first thought at being a prostitute was that if she was going to do it, she would be the best. Not a natural reaction. She was a definite Mary-Sue.<br /><br />This is actually the first book in a trilogy. Whether I continue remains to be seen.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18368524236327185335" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/460468618" />
    <a title="Sheena K" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7184921-sheena-k"><img alt="Sheena K" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356451861p2/7184921.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/460468618?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sheena K" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sheena K" href="/user/show/7184921-sheena-k">Sheena K</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer460468618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4804957635981045175">'Belle' has the potential to be much more, but the lacklustre writing, endless plot twists and thoroughly unlikable main character made it a tedious read.<br/><br/><br/> Subject matter is interesting and uncommon, but Belle as the main character ruins it for me. Her annoying naivety and eagerness to divulge her story to anyone she meets seems out of character for someone who has gone through so much at a young age. Also, her many failed attempts at escape get annoying after a while.<br/><br/><br/>Belle's mother, Annie, menti</span>
  <span id="freeText4804957635981045175" style="display:none">'Belle' has the potential to be much more, but the lacklustre writing, endless plot twists and thoroughly unlikable main character made it a tedious read.<br /><br /><br /> Subject matter is interesting and uncommon, but Belle as the main character ruins it for me. Her annoying naivety and eagerness to divulge her story to anyone she meets seems out of character for someone who has gone through so much at a young age. Also, her many failed attempts at escape get annoying after a while.<br /><br /><br />Belle's mother, Annie, mentioned that young girls forced into prostitution rarely, if ever get over the mental and emotional trauma. However, Belle doesn't seem to have changed one whit. She's pretty flat and static as a character. <br /><br /><br />Another thing I found annoying was that every time Lisette is mentioned, Pearse has to work in the fact that the lives of Lisette and her son will be in danger..etc. it gets tedious after the 2nd or 3rd repetition. <br /><br /><br />Pearse's writing style here is not cutting it for me (though I could be wrong, because I haven't read any of her other novels yet). Though I am not a big fan of purple prose, this lacks spice and subtlety. It is rather bland prose for such an exciting subject matter. <br /><br /><br />Frankly, I think that the setting of New Orleans was the best among the other places in the novel, and perhaps if the story were centred there with focus on the more fleshed out characters like Etienne, Lisette and Noah, it would have made for a more engaging read. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4804957635981045175" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_181824205" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/181824205" />
    <a title="Louise Graham" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5736994-louise-graham"><img alt="Louise Graham" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1394401105p2/5736994.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/181824205?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Louise Graham" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Louise Graham" href="/user/show/5736994-louise-graham">Louise Graham</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer181824205" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9527998420637260120">Belle is Lesley Pearse’s latest book set in 1910 in the East end of London. Right from the very beginning you are introduced to the main character Belle, who is a 15-year-old girl full of innocence despite living in the ground floors of her Mothers Brothel. Belle has no concept of what happens upstairs until one day she see something that changes her life for ever. <br/><br/>Belle’s whole world changes because of this one night. Snatched from the streets near her house and transported against her will int</span>
  <span id="freeText9527998420637260120" style="display:none">Belle is Lesley Pearse’s latest book set in 1910 in the East end of London. Right from the very beginning you are introduced to the main character Belle, who is a 15-year-old girl full of innocence despite living in the ground floors of her Mothers Brothel. Belle has no concept of what happens upstairs until one day she see something that changes her life for ever. <br /><br />Belle’s whole world changes because of this one night. Snatched from the streets near her house and transported against her will into a very sinister world where she has no control of her own fate. Only things she knows is that she must try to get back home and what ever cost. Along the way she meets many people, some good, some very surprising and some so nasty that you never see it coming.<br /><br />This book blew me away. I read it cover to cover, nearly 600 pages in one weekend. Lesley has an amazing ability to write about a subject that is so shocking that really you should put the book down yet you are so desperate to see Belle survive and have faith that something good will happen next (which isn’t always the case!). A rollercoaster of emotions.<br /><br />I was delighted to hear that this is not the end of the Belle saga. Belle’s War will be a follow-up (I believe next year). I have my own hopes for Belle but I know for certain what ever happens to her next I won’t be expecting it.<br /><br />Fantastic book Lesley – Thank you!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9527998420637260120" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Eha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47264375-eha"><img alt="Eha" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2763009877?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eha" href="/user/show/47264375-eha">Eha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2763009877" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2378413079513597855">This felt like a child’s imaginative playhouse story with adult content. <br/><br/>Within 30 pages I was wondering whether I should continue. I did, becuase the storyline was intriguing. I was aware that the content could well move into voyeuristic (as judged by me), but I did want to see where this author would take things. Montages moved quickly enough to keep me interested although I tended to skim the overwhelming number of scenes drawn out in graphic detail. <br/><br/>I found the writing style so bad and the “</span>
  <span id="freeText2378413079513597855" style="display:none">This felt like a child’s imaginative playhouse story with adult content. <br /><br />Within 30 pages I was wondering whether I should continue. I did, becuase the storyline was intriguing. I was aware that the content could well move into voyeuristic (as judged by me), but I did want to see where this author would take things. Montages moved quickly enough to keep me interested although I tended to skim the overwhelming number of scenes drawn out in graphic detail. <br /><br />I found the writing style so bad and the “character” development - wait, what characters? There weren’t characters. There were descriptions of e.v.e.r.y.one’s thoughts. Villains would get their backstory and inner thoughts described and then disappear. Belle was a cardboard cutout, first getting moved over here with this introspective paper dress and then getting moved over there wearing that capable paper outfit, waffling between “I can’t!” and “I have to!” <br /><br />As I said, it felt like a child moving her barbies around, but with adult content. Scenes were written in far too much detail, and the whole narrative couldn’t make up its mind whether it preferred the theory of ‘prostitution ought to be legalized and fun to take out the human trafficking bit’ or whether the whole experience was just one big trauma. <br /><br />I wish I hadn’t read it. I was going to put two stars so I’d feel better about my own waste of time. But no. It just keeps going down in stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2378413079513597855" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer680061732" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4906665435946461805">I've picked up this book because I didn't have a lot of choice then. A few chapters into the book, I was extremely shocked and sympathetic to Belle. To my surprised, it was really hard to put down the book. However, as the story progresses, I felt super depressed and frustrated as unfortunate events keep happening to Belle. There was a few times I wanted to stop reading. It seems to me that she claims to be good at reading people but keeps trusting the wrong people, which made me really sad. A f</span>
  <span id="freeText4906665435946461805" style="display:none">I've picked up this book because I didn't have a lot of choice then. A few chapters into the book, I was extremely shocked and sympathetic to Belle. To my surprised, it was really hard to put down the book. However, as the story progresses, I felt super depressed and frustrated as unfortunate events keep happening to Belle. There was a few times I wanted to stop reading. It seems to me that she claims to be good at reading people but keeps trusting the wrong people, which made me really sad. A few things that happened to her could have been prevented if she trust her own instincts. On the other hand, I was a bit disappointed with the ending. It is unrealistic for all the nice people succeed in helping Belle all of a sudden. The connection between the people seems too convenient. Throughout the book, Belle's relation to a lot of other people is explored and I was hoping to see something more emotional between Belle and her mother, especially of what they have both been through, and how her mother is indirectly the cause for the final incident that happens to Belle.</span>

  <span id="freeText3109821927194584040" style="display:none">I thought that the idea for the storyline was intriguing, however, the execution was quite poor. I found that there was a lot of repetition in the book, which made it a lot longer than it needed to be.<br /><br />I also found that the main character, Belle, was badly written. I just felt that for such a young girl, who experienced such terrible things, she bounced back awfully quickly, which I found a bit unrealistic.<br /><br />For example, it felt like 5 minutes after being sold into prostitution, she just goes, "I want to be the best and highest paid girl here!". That doesn't seem like an ordinary reaction to me. The character should have been a lot more damaged for me to sympathize with her, and take her a bit more seriously.<br /><br />I won't be buying the sequel.</span>

<div id="review_1197876753" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1197876753" />
    <a title="Resident Optimist" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3976871-resident-optimist"><img alt="Resident Optimist" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1378262010p2/3976871.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1197876753?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Resident Optimist" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Resident Optimist" href="/user/show/3976871-resident-optimist">Resident Optimist</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1197876753" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13373094180486021725">Page 202. Holy macaroni. The thing about long books is that they should be thoroughly captivating throughout. Unfortunately, I feel like much of the writing in this novel is just intended to fill pages and I mean that in the nicest way possible. I've read works by the same author before and have enjoyed them but not every book needs to be 600 pages long. Some variety is essential if you want to keep readers engaged. <br/><br/>Update: I ended up reading the rest of the book and I must say I ended up enjoyi</span>
  <span id="freeText13373094180486021725" style="display:none">Page 202. Holy macaroni. The thing about long books is that they should be thoroughly captivating throughout. Unfortunately, I feel like much of the writing in this novel is just intended to fill pages and I mean that in the nicest way possible. I've read works by the same author before and have enjoyed them but not every book needs to be 600 pages long. Some variety is essential if you want to keep readers engaged. <br /><br />Update: I ended up reading the rest of the book and I must say I ended up enjoying it more than I thought it would. Might I say; Etienne &lt;3. I've just found out that there are two more books in this series. I'm torn about reading them. I want to, purely to see Etienne again, but then I don't because I see that the other two books are whale sized too. Long books aren't a problem. Long books with poor editing are. I felt like every change in a scene was introduced with two pages of description. All that could have been cut out and we would have had a mighty fine book in our hands. I skim-read most of these sections and I can honestly say that I missed nothing. It's all fine to set the scene but not everything needs to be narrated. I'm a great fan of Ms Pearse and in my childhood I would devour her books - despite the fact that they were clearly not intended for my age group! It has taken me a while to realise however that this is a recurring problem with her books. I hope some sort of change is brought in because her story telling has some power to it, it just needs to be... condensed? <br /><br />I also had a massive problem with Belle. She was naive to the point of stupidity. I mean she was 15, not 5. Surely if she didn't know that her mother was running a whorehouse, she at least had SOME inkling as to what was going on upstairs? I find it near impossible to believe that anyone - especially anyone of that age could have been so naively blind. Also, Belle experiences some sort of personality overhaul after a series of ordeals. It isn't believable because it's one set of bad experiences that she goes through within a few days. For most people these experiences would scar them for life. Even the strongest and smartest of women wouldn't react the way Belle did. Belle decides to take her fate into her own hands and enjoy her ordeals. The transition that occurred there was not smooth at all. In fact, most of Belle's life was bumpy. <br /><br />Much of the book echoed scenes from Fanny Hill and was incredibly repetitive. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13373094180486021725" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8600331955429359253">It lies somewhere, where you can't tell it good or bad...probably after reading Trust me by Lesley, I expected a lot (and then again, the average GoodReads rating for Belle makes you expect a lot)..<br/><br/>Trust me was fatter, and still I completed it in flat 2 days...this one is a long one too (over 500 pages), but in this case they seem endless...in all honesty, by the last 70-80 pages, I was skimming the novel (something I hardly do)...<br/><br/>I don't know why this was written (given she is coming with it's </span>
  <span id="freeText8600331955429359253" style="display:none">It lies somewhere, where you can't tell it good or bad...probably after reading Trust me by Lesley, I expected a lot (and then again, the average GoodReads rating for Belle makes you expect a lot)..<br /><br />Trust me was fatter, and still I completed it in flat 2 days...this one is a long one too (over 500 pages), but in this case they seem endless...in all honesty, by the last 70-80 pages, I was skimming the novel (something I hardly do)...<br /><br />I don't know why this was written (given she is coming with it's sequel too!!) but then there was nothing inspiring or touching in this novel (I can't really be in awe of a gal surviving, rather thriving being a prostitute, someone who still has lot of people go gaga over her...there hardly was anything I can find worth liking in Belle...) And I don't know which category the novel comes...it's simply the life's journey of a gal (that too just a couple of year's account...rest is in sequel, I believe) but still, what was so great in this gal that we need her life account!!<br /><br />I had a list of Lesley's books to read...but reading this makes me put a comma, if not full stop, before I read any new one of hers...</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/179618743?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie Mcsweeney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie Mcsweeney" href="/user/show/4649093-katie-mcsweeney">Katie Mcsweeney</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4649093-katie-mcsweeney?shelf=history-historical-fiction">history-historical-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer179618743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5040146132228792738">Aw man... Why do I never love the high brow books?? I am a creature of low tastes! Such an easy read... not very well written but not badly written either. Pearse had a story to tell and she doesn't let fancy writing and literary constructs get in the way of her plot. Whatever about the simplicity of the writing Pearse does an amazing job of creating real, believable characters... an amazing job. They all felt so plausible, Kent, Sly, Mog, Annie, Johnny, Lisset... the list goes on...<br/>The book jum</span>
  <span id="freeText5040146132228792738" style="display:none">Aw man... Why do I never love the high brow books?? I am a creature of low tastes! Such an easy read... not very well written but not badly written either. Pearse had a story to tell and she doesn't let fancy writing and literary constructs get in the way of her plot. Whatever about the simplicity of the writing Pearse does an amazing job of creating real, believable characters... an amazing job. They all felt so plausible, Kent, Sly, Mog, Annie, Johnny, Lisset... the list goes on...<br />The book jumps around a fair bit which can be annoying but I think that is more my fault than hers! I wanted to know what Belle was up do and Pearse insisted on keeping us in the loop about what was going on in London.<br /><br />As for the ending I hated it. HATED IT! but it served its purpose as I cannot wait for "Belle's War" <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[in which I hope Johnny dies tragically at war and Etienne swoops in to save the day!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="5040146132228792738" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_473948812" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/473948812" />
    <a title="Freda Mans-Labianca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2967441-freda-mans-labianca"><img alt="Freda Mans-Labianca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576515308p2/2967441.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/473948812?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Freda Mans-Labianca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Freda Mans-Labianca" href="/user/show/2967441-freda-mans-labianca">Freda Mans-Labianca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2967441-freda-mans-labianca?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer473948812" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14771429626592072661">So very different from Stolen, and yet, just as wonderfully written.<br/>Belle is one of those books that you are rooting for her all the way, then at the end, you feel like chastising her for being so naive. <br/>I'm also not big on historical books, they really have to be interesting to pull me in completely, and Belle does just that. It's full of edge-of-the-seat moments, moments of terrifying empathy, moments that you hate to witness but are glad you didn't miss. It's full of so much, characters full </span>
  <span id="freeText14771429626592072661" style="display:none">So very different from Stolen, and yet, just as wonderfully written.<br />Belle is one of those books that you are rooting for her all the way, then at the end, you feel like chastising her for being so naive. <br />I'm also not big on historical books, they really have to be interesting to pull me in completely, and Belle does just that. It's full of edge-of-the-seat moments, moments of terrifying empathy, moments that you hate to witness but are glad you didn't miss. It's full of so much, characters full of life, scenes you thought you knew once, and drama you know you have heard of. <br />I really love how the author tells a story, no matter the genre or plot. She is talented enough to be about storytelling, and the intimate journey that pulls you deep into a book. Where you can't stop reading or talking about it.<br />I've only read these two books by her, and she has many, so I look forward to reading more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14771429626592072661" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer181008948" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5157723476055636053">Set in London in 1910, this is about Belle, who has grown up in a brothel where her mother is the madam, but been kept innocent of all that goes on until she witnesses the murder of one of the girls, and is then kidnapped by the killer and taken to France to be sold into prostitution. From there she is sold on to New Orleans and settles into a brothel where she becomes the top girl and learns to enjoy her profession. Meanwhile friends and family are trying to find out what happened to her. It's </span>
  <span id="freeText5157723476055636053" style="display:none">Set in London in 1910, this is about Belle, who has grown up in a brothel where her mother is the madam, but been kept innocent of all that goes on until she witnesses the murder of one of the girls, and is then kidnapped by the killer and taken to France to be sold into prostitution. From there she is sold on to New Orleans and settles into a brothel where she becomes the top girl and learns to enjoy her profession. Meanwhile friends and family are trying to find out what happened to her. It's not a bad story, but the writing style is quite clunky and Belle isn't particularly believable as a character - the supporting characters are more interesting.<br />I hadn't read any Lesley Pearce books before, and probably wouldn't go out of my way to read more, although the sequel to this comes out next year and it would be good to find out what happens next..</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jDOp9JbityHKYgbr8W1h79C8a1m5RWQJwpcV5TtCDbhDI7hTNXOF4tXGO0/KWeuvM3YHJZs0xWglJUEMmkL37Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WRkCxBfSV8Adwj+IAMghgiKdIQG9g2M1fWWPWNmIY56WCRNjtENlAwJmAiw7/KvCwVdNfZ/ywlSa19uxeIiZyw==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/458937.Lesley_Pearse">About Lesley Pearse</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>

<a href="/author/show/458937.Lesley_Pearse"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1261863858p3/458937.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11184119814543549742">Lesley Pearse is one of the UK's best-loved novelists with fans across the globe and sales of over 2 million copies of her books to date. A true storyteller and a master of gripping storylines that keep the reader hooked from beginning to end, Pearse introduces you to characters that it is impossible not to care about or forget. There is no formula to her books or easily defined genre. Whether cri</span>
  <span id="freeText11184119814543549742" style="display:none">Lesley Pearse is one of the UK's best-loved novelists with fans across the globe and sales of over 2 million copies of her books to date. A true storyteller and a master of gripping storylines that keep the reader hooked from beginning to end, Pearse introduces you to characters that it is impossible not to care about or forget. There is no formula to her books or easily defined genre. Whether crime as in 'Till We Meet Again', historical adventure like 'Never Look Back', or the passionately emotive 'Trust Me', based on the true-life scandal of British child migrants sent to Australia in the post war period, she engages the reader completely.<br />Truth is often stranger than fiction and Lesley's life has been as packed with drama as her books. She was three when her mother died under tragic circumstances. Her father was away at sea and it was only when a neighbour saw Lesley and her brother playing outside without coats on that suspicion was aroused - their mother had been dead for some time. With her father in the Royal Marines, Lesley and her older brother spent three years in grim orphanages before her father remarried - a veritable dragon of an ex army nurse - and Lesley and her older brother were brought home again, to be joined by two other children who were later adopted by her father and stepmother, and a continuing stream of foster children. The impact of constant change and uncertainty in Lesley's early years is reflected in one of the recurring themes in her books: what happens to those who are emotionally damaged as children. It was an extraordinary childhood and in all her books, Lesley has skilfully married the pain and unhappiness of her early experiences with a unique gift for storytelling.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11184119814543549742" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
